## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv/dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t), with nonlinear terms extending beyond the simple linear harmonic oscillator.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Cubic damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v (nonlinear velocity-dependent forces)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric restoring force with damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity nonlinearity in damping)
- Coupled position-velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x**2 * v (cross-coupling terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x²) → asymmetric potential indicating broken spatial symmetry
- Velocity terms with sign-dependent magnitude (v·|v|, v³) → nonlinear drag modeling aerodynamic or fluid resistance
- Product terms x²·v or (1-x²)·v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillators (van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c·t) or cos(c·t) → external periodic driving force causing resonance phenomena
- Position multiplied by periodic time function x·cos(c·t) → parametric excitation leading to parametric resonance
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system where phase portrait fully characterizes dynamics
- Linear v term with negative coefficient → energy injection (negative damping) suggesting limit cycle behavior
- Rational functions of x like x/(1+c·x²) → bounded restoring force modeling saturation of spring stiffness

The basis functions are: **{v, v·x², x³, x·t, x}**

The key question for each candidate is whether it can represent the term `x·t` (linear in both x and t).

Now I need to check if candidates can produce `x·t`. The candidates use either:
